Not the best but it works. It also works when I mix Skin 79 and Etude House together. Neither one of these products have any fragant to it. Missha BB cream does have fragrant. It smells like baby powder-ish. It's not bad (it eventually goes away after after few hours); however, I really don't care for the smell. Some people actually like the fragrant (on youtube). My skin is very clear except for the capillary red spots around the nose and occasional black acne spots. So I don't really need a \\"heavy\\" coverage (I used Laura Bare Mineral and Mercier tinted moisturizure for a long time). However, with a bit of setting powder, Missha BB cream lasts almost all day. Plus of Missha BB cream, high SPF (maybe that why it seems more oily).<br />In summary, for medium coverage Missha (if you don't mind the fragrant), Etude House (if you don't have dry skin). For light coverage, Skin 79. Tips: even though, BB creams are all in one products, always wear moisturizures (=/- additional sun block) and setting powder. Even though, you can build for more coverage, but I'd not recommended b/c it will look very heavy. Also, buy from a reputable Ebay sellers. It is cheaper than amazon, around $11-13. Beware, fake products are out there (I do not understand this either b/c it's not every expensive, why do people make/sell fake products). I suspect that these products are \\"drug-store\\" brands in Korea. But since we can't get our hands on, we are paying a bit more. Next, I want to try Tony Molly CC cream.<br />As for American brands, Smash Box is heavy, almost like foundation. Dior BB creams are more of yellow tone and dark. Tarte is too powdery for my liking. Boscia is water base so it's nice; however, it's one shade and not recommended for darker than NC-35. Too Face gives a dewy/sheer/natural look and good for yellow tone skin.<br />Hope you will find a right products.

  302. I originally bought this a few months ago for my mom, but it was too light for her skin tone, so she gave it to me.<br /><br />I've tried 5 BB creams so far, and Missha's Perfect BB Cream ranks in at #2 (their Signature BB cream performed better for me). You only need a little bit to cover your cheeks, a little more for the forehead and chin. You can layer this up for more coverage, but I wouldn't recommend it because it can look really cakey. It has a faint fragrance, but nothing too jarring--and definitely not as strong as Garnier's BB cream. You can apply this with your hands, but make sure to warm it up first between your fingers, as this helps it spread better.<br /><br />Coverage: I'd put this as light to medium coverage. While it did a good job at covering my redness, it was not able to cover some acne scars on my chin and cheeks. It seemed to somewhat cover my dark undereye circles. The finish is natural -- matte and makes your skin look soft.<br /><br />Color: This is best for pale people. I'm usually between NC20-25 with cool undertones and this color works perfectly. However, it didn't work for my mom, I'd say she's around NC30.<br /><br />Lastability: If you don't top this off with finishing powder, it won't last very long. I got 4-5 hours of wear with this cream before it started getting oily and revealing my patchy skintone.<br /><br />Overall, this is a very good BB cream that looks best with pale skintones and offers a matte, clean finish. However, it does not last long and can look oily after a while; it also does not cover blemishes well.
